### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 1 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company that makes wildlife videos purchases camera equipment for $\$ 32,400$. The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, after which it is considered to have no monetary value. How much is the camera equipment worth 4 years after it is purchased?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 10,800$
  B: $\$ 16,200$
  C: $\$ 21,600$
  D: $\$ 29,700$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
Action: 
  The depreciation is linear, so we can use the straight-line depreciation formula: 
  depreciation per year = (initial value - salvage value) / useful life
  salvage value = $\$ 0$
  initial value = $\$ 32,400$
  useful life = 12 years
  depreciation per year = (32400 - 0) / 12 = $\$ 2,700$
  After 4 years, the equipment would have depreciated by 4 * $\$ 2,700$ = $\$ 10,800$
  The current value of the equipment = initial value - total depreciation
  current value = $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800$ = $\$ 21,600$
  Therefore, the answer is (C) $\$ 21,600$. Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  If the equipment depreciates at a constant rate, then it loses the same amount of value each year.
  If the equipment is worth $x$ dollars initially, then it will be worth $x-ky$ dollars after $y$ years, where $k$ is the depreciation rate per year.
  
Action: 
  The equipment depreciates for 12 years, so after 12 years, it is worth $0$ dollars.
  Let's call the initial value of the equipment $x$.
  After 4 years, the equipment has depreciated for 4 years, so it is worth $x-4k$ dollars.
  We know that after 12 years, the equipment is worth $0$ dollars, so we can set up the equation:
  $x-12k=0$
  Solving for $k$, we get $k=\frac{x}{12}$.
  We can substitute this value of $k$ into the equation for the value of the equipment after 4 years:
  $x-4k=x-4\left(\frac{x}{12}\right)=\frac{2}{3}x$
  Therefore, the equipment is worth $\frac{2}{3}x$ dollars after 4 years.
  We know that the equipment was purchased for $\$32,400$, so $x=\$32,400$.
  Substituting this value, we get:
  $\frac{2}{3}(32400)=\boxed{\$ 21,600}$
  
Answer: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  We need to find the value of the equipment 4 years after it is purchased.
  
Solution:
  Since the equipment depreciates at a constant rate, we can assume that the depreciation is linear.
  Let's call the initial value of the equipment V.
  After 12 years, the equipment will have no monetary value, so we can set up the following equation:
  V - 12d = 0, where d is the depreciation per year.
  Solving for d, we get d = V/12.
  So, the value of the equipment after t years is:
  V - td
  After 4 years, the value of the equipment is:
  V - 4d = V - 4(V/12) = V - V/3 = 2V/3
  We know that V = $\$ 32,400$, so
  2V/3 = 2($\text{\$ 32,400}$/3) = $\text{\$ 21,600}$
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, after which it is considered to have no monetary value.
  Let $V(t)$ be the value of the equipment $t$ years after it is purchased. Then, $V(t)$ is a linear function of $t$.
  We know that $V(0) = 32,400$ and $V(12) = 0$.
  Therefore, the slope of the line passing through $(0, 32,400)$ and $(12, 0)$ is $m = -2,700$.
  So, $V(t) = -2,700t + 32,400$.
Action: 
  To find the value of the equipment 4 years after it is purchased, we need to compute $V(4)$.
  $V(4) = -2,700(4) + 32,400 = 20,400$
  Answer: Answer("B")
Response 4:

  The camera equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, which means it loses the same amount of value each year.
  After 12 years, the camera equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  We need to find the value of the camera equipment 4 years after it is purchased.
  Let's assume that the camera equipment loses $x$ dollars in value each year.
  Then, the value of the camera equipment after 4 years is $32,400 - 4x$ dollars.
Action: Answer("B")  
Using the information above, we can set up the following equation to solve for $x$:
$12x = 32,400$
$x = 2,700$
Therefore, the value of the camera equipment after 4 years is $32,400 - 4x = 32,400 - 4(2,700) = 21,600$ dollars.
Hence, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C)}\ \$21,600}$.

  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.

  The value of the equipment after a certain number of years can be calculated using the formula: value = initial value - (depreciation rate * number of years * initial value)
  In this case, the initial value is $\$ 32,400$ and the number of years is 4.

  depreciation rate = (initial value - final value) / (number of years * initial value)
  Since the final value is zero, the depreciation rate is: depreciation rate = 1 / (12 years) = 0.0833
  Using the formula, the value of the equipment after 4 years is:
  value = 32,400 - (0.0833 * 4 * 32,400) = 32,400 - 10,800 = $21,600

Response 9:
Knowledge:
  The depreciation of the camera equipment is linear.
  After 12 years, the equipment is worth $0.
  The initial value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400$.
  We need to find the value of the equipment after 4 years.
  
Action: 
  We can model the depreciation of the equipment with a linear equation: $y = mx + b$, where $y$ is the value of the equipment, $x$ is the number of years since it was purchased, $m$ is the slope of the line (the rate of depreciation), and $b$ is the initial value of the equipment.
  
  We know that the equipment is worth $\$ 0$ after 12 years, so we can use the points $(0, 32400)$ and $(12, 0)$ to find the slope of the line:
  
  $m = \frac{0 - 32400}{12 - 0} = -2700$
  
  So the equation for the depreciation of the equipment is: $y = -2700x + 32400$
  
  To find the value of the equipment after 4 years, we can plug in $x = 4$:
  
  $y = -2700(4) + 32400 = 21600$
  
  Therefore, the equipment is worth $\$ 21,600$ after 4 years.
  
  Answer: Answer("C")

Question: $$\frac{a-b}{a}=c$$In the equation above, if $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: $c>1$
  B: $c=1$
  C: $c=-1$
  D: $c<-1$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  We can simplify the equation above as follows:
  $$\frac{a-b}{a}=c \Rightarrow 1-\frac{b}{a}=c \Rightarrow 1-c=\frac{b}{a}$$
  Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, we know that $\frac{b}{a}$ is negative.
  A: If $c>1$, then $1-c$ is negative, which means that $\frac{b}{a}$ is negative, but this is not possible since $b$ is positive and $a$ is negative.
  B: If $c=1$, then $1-c=0$, which means that $\frac{b}{a}=0$, but this is not possible since $b$ is positive and $a$ is negative.
  C: If $c=-1$, then $1-c=2$, which means that $\frac{b}{a}$ is positive, but this is not possible since $b$ is positive and $a$ is negative.
  D: If $c<-1$, then $1-c$ is positive, which means that $\frac{b}{a}$ is positive, but this is not possible since $b$ is positive and $a$ is negative.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  To solve the equation, we can first multiply both sides by $a$ to get $a-b=ac$. 
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is negative.
  If $a\neq 0$, then we can divide both sides by $a$ to get $1-\frac{b}{a}=c$.
  If $a<0$ and $b>0$, then $1-\frac{b}{a}>1$.
  A: $c>1$ is not necessarily true.
  B: $c=1$ is not true since $1-\frac{b}{a}>1$.
  C: $c=-1$ is not true since $1-\frac{b}{a}$ is positive.
  D: $c<-1$ is true since $1-\frac{b}{a}>1$ and $c=\frac{a-b}{a}<0$.
Action: Answer("D")

$$a-b=ac$$

  $$\frac{b}{-a}<1$$
  $$\frac{a}{b}>1$$
  $$1-\frac{b}{a}<0$$
  $$c<1$$

Action:

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 5 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A cylindrical can containing pieces of fruit is filled to the top with syrup before being sealed. The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, and the height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$. If $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ of syrup is needed to fill the can to the top, which of the following is closest to the total volume of the pieces of fruit in the can?
Choices:
  A: $7.5 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  B: $185 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The volume of a cylinder is given by the formula: $V = \pi r^{2}h$, where $r$ is the radius of the base and $h$ is the height of the cylinder.

  The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$ and the height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$.
  The volume of the syrup in the can is equal to the volume of the cylinder minus the volume of the fruit in the can.

  The volume of the cylinder can be found by substituting the values into the formula: $V_{\text{cylinder}} = \pi r^{2}h = \pi \times 4.33^{2} \times 10 \approx 592.73 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The volume of the fruit in the can can be found by subtracting the volume of the syrup from the volume of the cylinder: $V_{\text{fruit}} = V_{\text{cylinder}} - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} \approx 482.73 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.

Question: If $y=k x$, where $k$ is a constant, and $y=24$ when $x=6$, what is the value of $y$ when $x=5$ ?
Choices:
  A: 6
  B: 15
  C: 20
  D: 23
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If $y=k x$, then $k$ is the slope of the line.
  If $y=24$ when $x=6$, then $k=24/6=4$.
Action: 
  Substituting $k=4$ and $x=5$ into the equation $y=kx$, we get $y=4\times5=20$.

Question: $$\begin{array}{r}3 x+4 y=-23 \\2 y-x=-19\end{array}$$What is the solution $(x, y)$ to the system of equations above?
Choices:
  A: $(-5,-2)$
  B: $(3,-8)$
  C: $(4,-6)$
  D: $(9,-6)$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  To solve the system of equations, we can use substitution or elimination method. In this case, we can use the elimination method by multiplying the second equation by 3 and adding it to the first equation to eliminate the variable x.
  
  $$
  \begin{array}{c}
  \begin{aligned}
  3 x+4 y=&-23 \\
  -3 x+6 y=&-57
  \end{aligned}
  \end{array}
  $$
  
  Adding the two equations, we get:
  
  $$
  10 y=-80
  $$
  
  Solving for y, we get:
  
  $$
  y=-8
  $$
  
  Substituting y into the second equation, we get:
  
  $$
  2(-8)-x=-19
  $$
  
  Solving for x, we get:
  
  $$
  x=3
  $$
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: To solve this system of equations, we can use substitution or elimination method. Let's use the elimination method in this case. We can multiply the second equation by 3 and add it to the first equation to eliminate x. Then we can solve for y and substitute back to find x.
$$\begin{array}{r}3 x+4 y=-23 \\2 y-x=-19\end{array}$$
$$\begin{array}{r}3x+4y=-23 \\9y-3x=-57\end{array}$$
Adding the two equations, we get:
$$13y=-80$$
$$y=-\frac{80}{13}$$
Substituting y back into the second equation, we get:
$$2(-\frac{80}{13})-x=-19$$
$$x=\frac{54}{13}$$

Context: $$.a=1,052+1.08 t.$$.The speed of a sound wave in air depends on the air temperature. The formula above shows the relationship between $a$, the speed of a sound wave, in feet per second, and $t$, the air temperature, in degrees Fahrenheit $\left({ }^{\circ} \mathrm{F}\right)$.
Question: Which of the following expresses the air temperature in terms of the speed of a sound wave?
Choices:
  A: $t=\frac{a-1,052}{1.08}$
  B: $t=\frac{a+1,052}{1.08}$
  C: $t=\frac{1,052-a}{1.08}$
  D: $t=\frac{1.08}{a+1,052}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The formula $a=1,052+1.08 t$ relates the speed of a sound wave $a$ in feet per second to the air temperature $t$ in degrees Fahrenheit.
  
Action: Answer("A")

$$a=1,052+1.08 t$$
$$a-1,052=1.08 t$$
$$\frac{a-1,052}{1.08}=t$$

Therefore, the expression that expresses the air temperature $t$ in terms of the speed of a sound wave $a$ is $t=\frac{a-1,052}{1.08}$. So, the answer is (A).

  B: 1
  C: $\frac{12}{7}$
  D: 3

$$6x-5=2x+7$$

$$x=3$$

Question: If $x>3$, which of the following is equivalent to $\frac{1}{\frac{1}{x+2}+\frac{1}{x+3}}$ ?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{2 x+5}{x^{2}+5 x+6}$
  B: $\frac{x^{2}+5 x+6}{2 x+5}$
  C: $2 x+5$
  D: $x^{2}+5 x+6$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  We can simplify $\frac{1}{\frac{1}{x+2}+\frac{1}{x+3}}$ by using the formula $\frac{1}{a+b}=\frac{1}{a}+\frac{1}{b}$.
  If we apply the formula, we get:
  $\frac{1}{\frac{1}{x+2}+\frac{1}{x+3}} = \frac{(x+2)(x+3)}{(x+2)+(x+3)} = \frac{(x+2)(x+3)}{2x+5}$.
  A: $\frac{2 x+5}{x^{2}+5 x+6}$ is not equivalent to $\frac{(x+2)(x+3)}{2x+5}$.
  B: $\frac{x^{2}+5 x+6}{2 x+5}$ is equivalent to $\frac{(x+2)(x+3)}{2x+5}$.
  C: $2 x+5$ is not equivalent to $\frac{(x+2)(x+3)}{2x+5}$.
  D: $x^{2}+5 x+6$ is not equivalent to $\frac{(x+2)(x+3)}{2x+5}$.

  C: This is not equivalent to the original expression.
  D: This is not equivalent to the original expression.

Action: Answer("D")

$$-ab + 15a = -9 \quad\Rightarrow\quad b = \frac{9 + 15a}{a} = \frac{9 + 15(4)}{4} = \frac{69}{4}$$

Question: Shipping Charges\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$\begin{array}{c}\text { Merchandise weight } \\ \text { (pounds) }\end{array}$ & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Shipping } \\ \text { charge }\end{array}$ \\\hline5 & $\$ 16.94$ \\\hline10 & $\$ 21.89$ \\\hline20 & $\$ 31.79$ \\\hline40 & $\$ 51.59$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows shipping charges for an online retailer that sells sporting goods. There is a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise. Which function can be used to determine the total shipping charge $f(x)$, in dollars, for an order with a merchandise weight of $x$ pounds?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=0.99 x$
  B: $f(x)=0.99 x+11.99$
  C: $f(x)=3.39 x$
  D: $f(x)=3.39 x+16.94$
Response 0:

  The function of a line in slope-intercept form is $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  The slope is the rate of change of the dependent variable (shipping charge) with respect to the independent variable (merchandise weight).

Choices:
  A: $w=30 A-4$
  B: $w=30 A+4$
  C: $w=30(A-4)$
  D: $w=30(A+4)$

  $w=30A-4$

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 18 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $a$ & $3 a$ & $5 a$ \\\hline$y$ & 0 & $-a$ & $-2 a$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of $x$ and their corresponding values of $y$ are shown in the table above, where $a$ is a constant. If there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, which of the following equations represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $x+2 y=a$
  B: $x+2 y=5 a$
  C: $2 x-y=-5 a$
  D: $2 x-y=7 a$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  A linear relationship between $x$ and $y$ can be represented by an equation of the form $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope of the line and $b$ is the $y$-intercept.
  Given two points $(x_1,y_1)$ and $(x_2,y_2)$ on a line, the slope of the line is given by $m=\frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$.
  The $y$-intercept of a line is the value of $y$ when $x=0$.
  
We can use the table to find two points on the line and then use those points to find the equation of the line.

Let's use the first and third rows of the table to find two points on the line.
The first row gives us the point $(x,a)$, and the third row gives us the point $(x, -2a)$.
The slope of the line passing through these two points is $m=\frac{-2a-a}{5a- a}=-\frac{3}{4}$.
The $y$-intercept of the line is given by the value of $y$ when $x=0$, which is $y=-a$.

So the equation of the line is $y=-\frac{3}{4}x-a$.

Now we need to check which of the given equations is equivalent to $y=-\frac{3}{4}x-a$.

A: $x+2y=a$
If we solve for $y$ in terms of $x$, we get $y=\frac{1}{2}a-\frac{1}{2}x$. This is not equivalent to $y=-\frac{3}{4}x-a$.

B: $x+2y=5a$
If we solve for $y$ in terms of $x$, we get $y=\frac{5}{2}a-\frac{1}{2}x$. This is not equivalent to $y=-\frac{3}{4}x-a$.

C: $2x-y=-5a$
If we solve for $y$ in terms of $x$, we get $y=2x+5a$. This is not equivalent to $y=-\frac{3}{4}x-a$.

D: $2x-y=7a$
If we solve for $y$ in terms of $x$, we get $y=2x-7a$. This is equivalent to $y=-\frac{3}{4}x-a$.

Therefore, the answer is $\textbf{(D)}$.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  If there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, then the equation that represents the relationship will be of the form $y = mx + b$, where $m$ is the slope of the line and $b$ is the $y$-intercept.
  We can find the slope of the line by choosing any two points from the table and using the formula $m = \frac{\text{change in }y}{\text{change in }x}$.
  Once we have the slope, we can find the $y$-intercept by plugging in the coordinates of one of the points and solving for $b$ in the equation $y = mx + b$.
  
Action:
  Let's choose the points $(a,0)$ and $(3a,-a)$ from the table.
  The slope of the line is $m = \frac{\text{change in }y}{\text{change in }x} = \frac{-a - 0}{3a - a} = \frac{-a}{2a} = -\frac{1}{2}$.
  Plugging in the coordinates of the point $(a,0)$, we get $0 = -\frac{1}{2}a + b$, so $b = \frac{1}{2}a$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $y = -\frac{1}{2}x + \frac{1}{2}a$.
  We can rewrite this equation as $x + 2y = 2a$, or $x + 2y = 5a - 3a$.
  This matches choice $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}}$.

  Therefore, the answer is B: $x+2y=5a$.

  Using the point-slope form of the equation of a line with the point $(a,0)$, we get:
  $y - 0 = -\frac{1}{2}(x - a)$
  Simplifying, we get:
  $y = -\frac{1}{2}x + \frac{1}{2}a$

  $2y = -x + a$
  Adding $x$ to both sides, we get:
  $x + 2y = a$

  We can use the values in the table to find the slope of the line that relates $x$ and $y$.

Action: 
  The slope of the line that relates $x$ and $y$ is equal to the change in $y$ divided by the change in $x$. We can see that the change in $x$ from $a$ to $3a$ is $2a$, and the corresponding change in $y$ from $0$ to $-a$ is $-a$. Therefore, the slope of the line is $\frac{-a}{2a}=-\frac{1}{2}$. 
  We can also find the $y$-intercept of the line by looking at the table. When $x=5a$, we have $y=-2a$. Therefore, the $y$-intercept is $-2a$.
  The equation of the line in slope-intercept form is $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the $y$-intercept. Substituting $m=-\frac{1}{2}$ and $b=-2a$, we get $y=-\frac{1}{2}x-2a$.
  To put this equation in the form $ax+by=c$, we can multiply both sides by $-2$ to get $-2y=x+4a$, or $x+2y=4a$.
  Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(D)}\ 2x-y=7a}$.

Question: $$\begin{aligned}1 \text { decagram } & =10 \text { grams } \\1,000 \text { milligrams } & =1 \text { gram }\end{aligned}$$A hospital stores one type of medicine in 2-decagram containers. Based on the information given in the box above, how many 1-milligram doses are there in one 2-decagram container?
Choices:
  A: $\quad 0.002$
  B: $\quad 200$
  C: $\quad 2,000$
  D: 20,000
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  1 decagram = 10 grams
  1,000 milligrams = 1 gram
  We want to find how many 1-milligram doses are there in one 2-decagram container.
  1 decagram = 10000 milligrams (by using the above conversions)
  2 decagrams = 20000 milligrams (by multiplying 10000 by 2)
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
We need to convert 2 decagrams to milligrams, and then divide by 1 milligram to find the number of doses. 

First, we convert 2 decagrams to grams: 

$$2 \text{ decagrams } = 2 \cdot 10 \text{ grams/decagram } = 20 \text{ grams}$$

Next, we convert 20 grams to milligrams: 

$$20 \text{ grams } = 20 \cdot 1000 \text{ milligrams/gram } = 20,000 \text{ milligrams}$$

Finally, we divide 20,000 milligrams by 1 milligram per dose: 

$$\frac{20,000 \text{ milligrams}}{1 \text{ milligram/dose}} = 20,000 \text{ doses}$$

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(D) }20,000}$.

1 gram = 1000 milligrams

A 2-decagram container would therefore contain:

2 decagrams = 2 $\times$ 10,000 milligrams = 20,000 milligrams.

Each dose is 1 milligram, so the number of 1-milligram doses in one 2-decagram container would be:

$\frac{20,000 \text{ milligrams}}{1 \text{ milligram/dose}} = 20,000$ doses.

Answer: $\boxed{\textbf{(D) }20,000}$.

Choices:
  A: -2
  B: 0
  C: 1
  D: 2
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  $h(x)=1-g(x)$
  $g(x)=2x-1$
Action: Answer("C")  

To find $h(0)$, we substitute $x=0$ into the expression for $h(x)$: 

$$h(0)=1-g(0)$$

Now we need to find $g(0)$:

$$g(0)=2(0)-1=-1$$

So, 

$$h(0)=1-g(0)=1-(-1)=2$$

Therefore, the answer is (C) 1.
Response 1:

Question: $$y=-(x-3)^{2}+a$$In the equation above, $a$ is a constant. The graph of the equation in the $x y$-plane is a parabola. Which of the following is true about the parabola?
Choices:
  A: Its minimum occurs at $(-3, a)$.
  B: Its minimum occurs at $(3, a)$.
  C: Its maximum occurs at $(-3, a)$.
  D: Its maximum occurs at $(3, a)$.
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The equation given is in vertex form: $y=a-(x-h)^2$, where $(h,k)$ is the vertex of the parabola.
  The negative sign in front of the squared term means that the parabola opens downward.
  The vertex of the parabola is $(3,a)$.
  Therefore, the minimum value of $y$ occurs at $(3,a)$.
Action: Answer("B")

Topic: Math
Question: A psychologist set up an experiment to study the tendency of a person to select the first item when presented with a series of items. In the experiment, 300 people were presented with a set of five pictures arranged in random order. Each person was asked to choose the most appealing picture. Of the first 150 participants, 36 chose the first picture in the set. Among the remaining 150 participants, $p$ people chose the first picture in the set. If more than $20 \%$ of all participants chose the first picture in the set, which of the following inequalities best describes the possible values of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: $p>0.20(300-36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  B: $p>0.20(300+36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  C: $p-36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
  D: $p+36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
Let $x$ be the number of people who chose the first picture in the set. We know that $x$ is greater than 20% of 300, which is 60. So $x>60$.

Of the first 150 participants, 36 chose the first picture. This means that among the first 150 participants, $36/150 = 0.24$ or 24% chose the first picture. 

We also know that among the remaining 150 participants, $p$ chose the first picture. 

Action: 
The total number of people who chose the first picture is $36+p$. 

We want to find the range of possible values of $p$ such that more than 20% of all participants chose the first picture. 

Since we know that $x>60$, we can say that $36+p > 60$. 

Simplifying this inequality, we get $p > 24$. 

We also know that $p$ is less than or equal to 150 (since there were only 150 remaining participants). 

Therefore, the best inequality that describes the possible values of $p$ is: 

$p > 24$, where $p \leq 150$

Answer: $\boxed{\textbf{(D)}\ p+36>0.20(300)\text{, where }p \leq 150}$

Solution:

$$

$$
which is equivalent to
$$
p > 24.
$$

Question: In the $x y$-plane, the line determined by the points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ passes through the origin. Which of the following could be the value of $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 4
  C: 8
  D: 16
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The equation of a line passing through two points $(x_1,y_1)$ and $(x_2,y_2)$ is given by:
  $y-y_1 = \frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}(x-x_1)$
  The line passes through the origin if $y_1=0$ and $x_1=0$. 
  We can plug in $(x_1,y_1)=(0,0)$ and $(x_2,y_2)=(2,k)$ to get:
  $y-kx/2=0$
  Similarly, plugging in $(x_1,y_1)=(0,0)$ and $(x_2,y_2)=(k,32)$ gives:
  $32-kx/2=0$
  Solving for $k$ gives $k=0$ or $k=64/x$
  A: If $k=0$, then the line passes through the origin, which satisfies the condition.
  B: If $k=4$, then $k\neq 64/x$ for any $x$, so the line does not pass through the origin.
  C: If $k=8$, then $k\neq 64/x$ for any $x$, so the line does not pass through the origin.
  D: If $k=16$, then $k=64/x$ when $x=4$, so the line does not pass through the origin.

  The slope of a line passing through two points $(x_1,y_1)$ and $(x_2,y_2)$ is given by $m = \frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$.
  If a line passing through two points $(x_1,y_1)$ and $(x_2,y_2)$ has a $y$-intercept of 0, then $y_1 = m x_1$ and $y_2 = m x_2$.

  Simplifying this equation gives $k=0$ or $k=8$.

  B: If $k=4$, then the line has equation $y=\frac{8}{3}x$, which passes through the origin.
  C: If $k=8$, then the line has equation $y=4x$, which passes through the origin.
  D: If $k=16$, then the line has equation $y=\frac{2}{3}x$, which does not pass through the origin.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 9:
Knowledge:
  A line that passes through the origin has the equation $y = mx$ where $m$ is the slope of the line.
  The slope of a line passing through the points $(x_1,y_1)$ and $(x_2,y_2)$ is given by $m = \frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}$.
  Using the points $(2,k)$ and $(k,32)$, we can find the slope of the line that passes through them.
  The slope of the line that passes through $(2,k)$ and $(k,32)$ is $\frac{32 - k}{k - 2}$.
  If this line passes through the origin, then the point $(0,0)$ must be on the line, so $y = 0$ when $x = 0$.
  Therefore, we have $\frac{32 - k}{k - 2} = 0$, which implies that $k = 32$ or $k = 2$.

Question: If 50 one-cent coins were stacked on top of each other in a column, the column would be approximately $3 \frac{7}{8}$ inches tall. At this rate, which of the following is closest to the number of one-cent coins it would take to make an 8-inch-tall column?
Choices:
  A: 75
  B: 100
  C: 200
  D: 390
Response 0:

  - The height of each coin is not given.
  - The height of 50 coins is $3 \frac{7}{8}$ inches.
  - We are asked to find the number of coins in an 8-inch-tall column.
  
Calculation:
  - Let's find the height of one coin: $\frac{3\frac{7}{8}}{50} \approx 0.0775$ inches.
  - To find the number of coins in an 8-inch-tall column, we divide 8 by the height of one coin: $\frac{8}{0.0775} \approx 103.23$.
  
Action: Answer("B")

  Therefore, we can say that $50:3 \frac{7}{8} = 100:7 \frac{3}{4}$.

Question: Percent of Residents Who Earned a Bachelor's Degree or Higher\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hlineState & Percent of residents \\\hlineState A & $21.9 \%$ \\\hlineState B & $27.9 \%$ \\\hlineState C & $25.9 \%$ \\\hlineState D & $19.5 \%$ \\\hlineState E & $30.1 \%$ \\\hlineState F & $36.4 \%$ \\\hlineState G & $35.5 \%$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}A survey was given to residents of all 50 states asking if they had earned a bachelor's degree or higher.The results from 7 of the states are given in the table above. The median percent of residents who earned a bachelor's degree or higher for all 50 states was $26.95 \%$. What is the difference between the median percent of residents who earned a bachelor's degree or higher for these 7 states and the median for all 50 states?
Choices:
  A: $0.05 \%$
  B: $0.95 \%$
  C: $1.22 \%$
  D: $7.45 \%$
Response 0:
To find the median of the 7 states, we need to order the percent of residents who earned a bachelor's degree or higher from least to greatest: 

$19.5 \%$, $21.9 \%$, $25.9 \%$, $27.9 \%$, $30.1 \%$, $35.5 \%$, $36.4 \%$

The median is the middle value, which is $27.9 \%$. 

To find the difference between the median of these 7 states and the median for all 50 states, we subtract the two values: 

$26.95 \% - 27.9 \% = -0.95 \%$

However, the question asks for the absolute value of the difference, so we take the positive value: 

$| -0.95 \% | = 0.95 \%$

Therefore, the answer is $\textbf{(B)}\ 0.95 \%$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 30 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{c|c}Year & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Subscriptions } \\ \text { sold }\end{array}$ \\\hline2012 & 5,600 \\2013 & 5,880 \\\end{tabular}\end{center}The manager of an online news service received the report above on the number of subscriptions sold by the service. The manager estimated that the percent increase from 2012 to 2013 would be double the percent increase from 2013 to 2014 . How many subscriptions did the manager expect would be sold in 2014 ?
Choices:
  A: 6,020
  B: 6,027
  C: 6,440
  D: 6,468 DIRECTIONS
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - To find the percent increase from year A to year B, use the formula: 
    percent increase = $\frac{\text{amount of increase}}{\text{original amount}} \times 100\%$
  - To find the amount of increase, use the formula:
    amount of increase = new amount - original amount
  - If x is the percent increase from 2013 to 2014, then the percent increase from 2012 to 2013 is x/2.
  - The number of subscriptions sold in 2014 is equal to the number sold in 2013 plus the amount of increase from 2013 to 2014.

Action: 
  Let's first find the percent increase from 2013 to 2014. We can use the formula:
  percent increase = $\frac{\text{amount of increase}}{\text{original amount}} \times 100\%$
  percent increase from 2013 to 2014 = $\frac{N_\text{2014} - N_\text{2013}}{N_\text{2013}} \times 100\%$, where $N_\text{2013}$ is the number of subscriptions sold in 2013 and $N_\text{2014}$ is the number of subscriptions sold in 2014.
  Substituting the given values, we get:
  percent increase from 2013 to 2014 = $\frac{N_\text{2014} - 5880}{5880} \times 100\%$
  
  Let's now find the percent increase from 2012 to 2013. We know that this is half of the percent increase from 2013 to 2014. So:
  percent increase from 2012 to 2013 = $\frac{1}{2} \times$ percent increase from 2013 to 2014
  
  Now we can set up an equation to solve for $N_\text{2014}$:
  $N_\text{2014} = N_\text{2013} + \text{amount of increase from 2013 to 2014}$
  $N_\text{2014} = 5880 + (\frac{1}{2} \times \frac{N_\text{2014} - 5880}{5880} \times 100\%) \times 5880$
  Solving for $N_\text{2014}$:
  $N_\text{2014} = 6068.4$
  
  Since $N_\text{2014}$ is a number of subscriptions, we should round it to the nearest whole number. 
  The closest answer choice is B: 6,027.
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The percent increase from 2012 to 2013 is: ((5880-5600)/5600)*100% = 5%
  - Let x be the number of subscriptions sold in 2014.
  - The percent increase from 2013 to 2014 is: ((x-5880)/5880)*100%
  - The manager estimated that the percent increase from 2012 to 2013 would be double the percent increase from 2013 to 2014.
  - Mathematically, this can be expressed as: 2 * 5% = ((x-5880)/5880)*100%
Action: 
  Let's first solve for x using the equation: 2 * 5% = ((x-5880)/5880)*100%
  Simplifying, we get: x = 6174
  Therefore, the manager expected 6,174 subscriptions to be sold in 2014, which is closest to answer choice D: 6,468. 
  However, none of the answer choices match exactly, so the best answer is D.

  Let S1 be the number of subscriptions sold in 2012, and let S2 be the number of subscriptions sold in 2013.

  The expected percent increase from 2012 to 2013 is double the percent increase from 2013 to 2014. This can be written as: r1 = 2 * r2
  The expected number of subscriptions sold in 2014 can be computed using the formula: S_2014 = S_2013 * (1 + r2)
  
Solution:
  r1 = (5,880 - 5,600) / 5,600 * 100% = 5%
  r2 = r1 / 2 = 2.5%
  S_2014 = 5,880 * (1 + 2.5%) = 6,027

Question: A customer paid $\$ 53.00$ for a jacket after a 6 percent sales tax was added. What was the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 47.60$
  B: $\$ 50.00$
  C: $\$ 52.60$
  D: $\$ 52.84$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The price of the jacket before the sales tax was added can be found by dividing the total price by 1 plus the tax rate as follows: price_before_tax = price_after_tax / (1 + tax_rate)
  In this case, the tax rate is 6% or 0.06.
Action: 
  price_before_tax = 53 / (1 + 0.06) = 50
  Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  "6 percent sales tax" means that the tax rate is 6% of the original price of the jacket.
  The amount of the tax is calculated by multiplying the original price of the jacket by 6%.
  The total amount paid by the customer is the sum of the original price of the jacket and the amount of the tax.
  A: $\$ 47.60$ is the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added if there was no discount. 
  B: $\$ 50.00$ is not the correct answer because it is the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added if there was a 6% discount.
  C: $\$ 52.60$ is not the correct answer because it is the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added if the tax rate was 5.6%.
  D: $\$ 52.84$ is not the correct answer because it is not one of the available choices.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 36 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company purchased a machine valued at $\$ 120,000$. The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year so that after 10 years the value will be $\$ 30,000$. Which of the following equations gives the value, $v$, of the machine, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased for $0 \leq t \leq 10 ?$
Choices:
  A: $v=30,000-9,000 t$
  B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$
  C: $v=120,000+9,000 t$
  D: $v=120,000-30,000 t$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year.
  After 10 years the value of the machine will be $\$ 30,000$.
  The initial value of the machine is $\$ 120,000$.
  
Solution:
  Let $d$ be the amount of the depreciation per year.
  Then, the value of the machine $t$ years after it was purchased is $v=120,000-dt$.
  We know that after 10 years, the value of the machine is $\$ 30,000$. So, we have:
  \begin{align*}
  v &= 120,000 - 10d \\
  30,000 &= 120,000 - 10d \\
  10d &= 90,000 \\
  d &= 9,000 \\
  \end{align*}
  Therefore, the equation that gives the value $v$ of the machine, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased is:
  \begin{align*}
  v &= 120,000 - 9,000 t \\
  \end{align*}
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year.
  After 10 years the value will be $\$ 30,000$.
  The initial value of the machine is $\$ 120,000$.
  
Solution:
  Since the value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year, we can find the rate of depreciation by taking the difference of the initial value and the final value, and dividing it by the number of years:
  $$\frac{120,000-30,000}{10}=9,000$$
  So, the value of the machine, $v$, $t$ years after it was purchased can be expressed as:
  $$v=120,000-9,000t$$

We can use the point-slope form of a linear equation to solve the problem. Let $m$ be the slope of the line (the amount that the value decreases each year), and let $(x_1, y_1) = (0, 120000)$ be a point on the line (the initial value of the machine). Then the equation of the line is given by $y - y_1 = m(x - x_1)$. We can use the fact that after 10 years, the value of the machine will be $\$ 30,000$ to find the slope, $m$.

$30,000 - 120,000 = -90,000$, so the value of the machine decreases by $\$ 9,000$ each year. Therefore, $m = -9,000$.

Now we can substitute $m$ and $(x_1, y_1)$ into the equation of the line to get the equation of the value of the machine, $v$, as a function of time, $t$.

$y - y_1 = m(x - x_1)$
$v - 120,000 = -9,000(t - 0)$
$v = -9,000t + 120,000$

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 37 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& x=y-3 \\& \frac{x}{2}+2 y=6\end{aligned}$$Which ordered pair $(x, y)$ satisfies the system of equations shown above?
Choices:
  A: $(-3,0)$
  B: $(0,3)$
  C: $(6,-3)$
  D: $(36,-6)$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
We are given a system of equations with two variables x and y. We can solve for x in the first equation and substitute it into the second equation to solve for y. Once we have the value of y, we can substitute it back into the first equation to find the value of x. 

Solution:
$$\begin{aligned}& x=y-3 \\& \frac{x}{2}+2 y=6\end{aligned}$$
Substitute x in the second equation with the expression for x from the first equation:
$$\frac{y-3}{2}+2y=6$$
Simplify and solve for y:
$$\begin{aligned}&\frac{y-3}{2}+2y=6\\
\Rightarrow &y-3+4y=12\\
\Rightarrow &5y=15\\
\Rightarrow &y=3\end{aligned}$$
Substitute y=3 back into the first equation to find x:
$$x=3-3=0$$
So the ordered pair $(x,y)$ that satisfies the system of equations is $(0,3)$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:

$$\frac{x}{2}+2 y=6$$
$$\frac{y-3}{2}+2 y=6$$
$$\frac{y}{2}+2 y=9$$
$$\frac{5y}{2}=9$$
$$y=\frac{18}{5}$$

Then, we can use the first equation to solve for $x$.

$$x=y-3$$
$$x=\frac{18}{5}-3$$
$$x=-\frac{3}{5}$$

$$x=5-3=2$$

What is the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week?
Choices:
  A: 38
  B: 33
  C: 22
  D: 16
Response 0:

- He saves $90 \%$ of his earnings each week.
- We want to find the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$.
- We can set up an equation to solve for the number of hours he needs to work.
- The equation is: $0.9(8 \times 10 + 10x) \geq 270$, where $x$ is the number of hours he works after the first 10 hours.

Action: Answer("C")

$0.9(8 \times 10 + 10x) \geq 270$

$0.9(80 + 10x) \geq 270$

$72 + 9x \geq 270$

$9x \geq 198$

$x \geq 22$

Therefore, Ken needs to work at least 22 hours after the first 10 hours to save at least $\$ 270$.

$x \geq 22$

Question: A cargo helicopter delivers only 100-pound packages and 120-pound packages. For each delivery trip, the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages, and the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds. What is the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 4
  C: 5
  D: 6
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let x be the number of 100-pound packages, and y be the number of 120-pound packages.
  We are looking for the maximum value of y, subject to the following constraints:
  x + y >= 10   (the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages)
  100x + 120y <= 1100  (the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds)
  A: If the helicopter carries 2 packages of 120 pounds each, it can carry 8 packages of 100 pounds each, for a total weight of 2*120 + 8*100 = 1040 pounds, which is less than the limit of 1,100 pounds. Therefore, the helicopter can carry more packages, and more than 2 packages of 120 pounds each.
  B: If the helicopter carries 4 packages of 120 pounds each, it can carry 6 packages of 100 pounds each, for a total weight of 4*120 + 6*100 = 1080 pounds, which is less than the limit of 1,100 pounds. Therefore, the helicopter can carry more packages, and more than 4 packages of 120 pounds each.
  C: If the helicopter carries 5 packages of 120 pounds each, it can carry 5 packages of 100 pounds each, for a total weight of 5*120 + 5*100 = 1100 pounds, which is equal to the limit of 1,100 pounds. Therefore, this is the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip.
  D: If the helicopter carries 6 packages of 120 pounds each, it can carry 4 packages of 100 pounds each, for a total weight of 6*120 + 4*100 = 1180 pounds, which is more than the limit of 1,100 pounds. Therefore, the helicopter cannot carry 6 packages of 120 pounds each.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:

  The total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds, so 100x + 120y <= 1,100.
  
To maximize the number of 120-pound packages, we want to use as many 120-pound packages as possible while still satisfying the weight and quantity constraints.

Action: Answer("C")

Substituting this into the weight constraint, we get 100(10 - y) + 120y <= 1,100.
Simplifying the inequality, we get 1,000 - 20y + 120y <= 1,100, or 100y <= 100, or y <= 1.
Since y must be a non-negative integer, the maximum number of 120-pound packages is y = 5. Therefore, the answer is C: 5.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 45 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In the $x y$-plane, the parabola with equation $y=(x-11)^{2}$ intersects the line with equation $y=25$ at two points, $A$ and $B$. What is the length of $\overline{A B}$ ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 12
  C: 14
  D: 16
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The equation of a parabola of the form $y=a(x-h)^2+k$ has its vertex at $(h,k)$.
  If a parabola of the form $y=a(x-h)^2+k$ intersects a horizontal line $y=c$ at two points, then the distance between these two points is $2|k-c|/\sqrt{a}$.
  
Action: 
  The vertex of the parabola $y=(x-11)^2$ is $(11,0)$.
  Since the line $y=25$ is above the vertex of the parabola, the parabola will intersect the line at two points.
  The equation of the line $y=25$ is equivalent to $y-c=0(x-0)$ where $c=25$.
  Therefore, the distance between the two intersection points is $2|0-25|/\sqrt{1}=50$.
  Answer: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The parabola with equation $y = (x - h)^2 + k$ has vertex at $(h, k)$.
  The parabola with equation $y = (x - h)^2 + k$ is symmetric with respect to the vertical line $x = h$.
  The line with equation $y = a$ is a horizontal line located at $a$ units above the $x$-axis.
  To find the $x$-coordinates of the points of intersection between a parabola and a horizontal line, we can set the equation of the parabola equal to the $y$-coordinate of the horizontal line and solve for $x$.
Action: 
The equation of the parabola is $y = (x - 11)^2$. Setting $y = 25$, we get $(x - 11)^2 = 25$. Taking square roots, we get $x - 11 = \pm 5$, so $x = 6$ or $x = 16$. Therefore, the $x$-coordinates of points $A$ and $B$ are $6$ and $16$, respectively. The distance between $A$ and $B$ is $16 - 6 = 10$. Answer: $\boxed{\textbf{(A)}\ 10}$.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The equation of a parabola with vertex $(h,k)$ is $y-k=a(x-h)^2$, where $a$ is a constant that determines the shape of the parabola.
  The given parabola has vertex $(11,0)$ and opens upwards.
  The line $y=25$ is a horizontal line.
  The intersection points of the parabola and the line $y=25$ have the same $y$-coordinate of $25$.

Topic: Math
Question: Oil and gas production in a certain area dropped from 4 million barrels in 2000 to 1.9 million barrels in 2013. Assuming that the oil and gas production decreased at a constant rate, which of the following linear functions $f$ best models the production, in millions of barrels, $t$ years after the year 2000 ?
Choices:
  A: $f(t)=\frac{21}{130} t+4$
  B: $f(t)=\frac{19}{130} t+4$
  C: $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130} t+4$
  D: $f(t)=-\frac{19}{130} t+4$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  We can use the point-slope form of a linear equation to model the oil and gas production.
  The point-slope form of a linear equation is $y-y_1=m(x-x_1)$, where $m$ is the slope of the line and $(x_1,y_1)$ is a point on the line.
  We can use the two given data points $(0,4)$ and $(13,1.9)$ to find the slope of the line.
  The slope of the line is the rate of change of the oil and gas production per year.
  The slope of the line is $\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}=\frac{1.9-4}{13-0}=-\frac{21}{130}$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The problem is asking for a linear function that models the oil and gas production as a function of time, assuming that the production decreased at a constant rate. 
  The function should have the form $f(t) = mt + b$, where $m$ is the slope of the line and $b$ is the initial production in 2000. 
  We can find the slope $m$ by computing the change in production per year, which is equal to the total decrease in production (in millions of barrels) divided by the number of years between 2000 and 2013.
  The total decrease in production is $4 - 1.9 = 2.1$ million barrels, and the number of years between 2000 and 2013 is $13$. Therefore, the slope is $m = \frac{-2.1}{13} = -\frac{21}{130}$.
  The initial production in 2000 is given as 4 million barrels, so $b=4$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 47 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Townsend Realty purchased the Glenview Street property and received a $40 \%$ discount off the original price along with an additional $20 \%$ off the discounted price for purchasing the property in cash. Which of the following best approximates the original price, in dollars, of the Glenview Street property?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 350,000$
  B: $\$ 291,700$
  C: $\$ 233,300$
  D: $\$ 175,000$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The discount formula is: Discount = (Discount Rate) x (Original Price)
  - The formula for the final price after a discount is: Final Price = Original Price - Discount
  - If an item is discounted by $x \%$, then the customer pays $(100-x) \%$ of the original price.
  
Solution:
  Let P be the original price of the property.
  After the first discount, the price is 60% of P or 0.6P.
  After the second discount, the price is 80% of 0.6P or 0.48P.
  We know that the final price is 0.48P and that this price is equal to 60% of the original price, so we can set up the equation:
  
  0.48P = 0.6 * P
  
  Solving for P, we get:
  
  P = 0.48P / 0.6 = 0.8P
  
  Therefore, the original price was 1.25 times the final price.
  Let F be the final price, then we have:
  
  P = 1.25 * F
  
  We know that F is the price after the second discount, so:
  
  F = 0.8 * 0.6 * P = 0.48P
  
  Substituting F, we get:
  
  P = 1.25 * 0.48P = 0.6P
  
  Solving for P, we get:
  
  P =  $\frac{0.6P}{1-0.6} = 1.5P$
  
  Therefore, the original price was 1.5 times the final price.
  
  Let F be the final price, then we have:
  
  P = 1.5 * F
  
  We know that F is the price after the second discount, so:
  
  F = 0.8 * 0.6 * P = 0.48P
  
  Substituting F, we get:
  
  P = 1.5 * 0.48P = 0.72P
  
  Solving for P, we get:
  
  P = $\frac{0.72P}{1-0.72} = 2.57P$
  
  Therefore, the original price was 2.57 times the final price.
  
  Let F be the final price, then we have:
  
  P = 2.57 * F
  
  We know that F is the price after the second discount, so:
  
  F = 0.8 * 0.6 * P = 0.48P
  
  Substituting F, we get:
  
  P = 2.57 * 0.48P = 1.2336P
  
  Solving for P, we get:
  
  P = $\frac{1.2336P}{1-1.2336} = 168,000$
  
  Therefore, the original price of the property was approximately $\$168,000$.
  
Answer: Answer("None of the Above")

Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $f(x)$ \\\hline1 & 5 \\\hline3 & 13 \\\hline5 & 21 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of the linear function $f$ are shown in the table above. Which of the following defines $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=2 x+3$
  B: $f(x)=3 x+2$
  C: $f(x)=4 x+1$
  D: $f(x)=5 x$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  A linear function has the form $f(x)=mx+b$ where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the $y$-intercept.
  To find the slope of a linear function given two points $(x_1,y_1)$ and $(x_2,y_2)$, we use the formula $m=\frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$.
  We can use the slope-intercept form of a linear function to find the value of $b$ by plugging in the coordinates of one of the points and solving for $b$.
  
Solution:
  Using the points $(1,5)$ and $(3,13)$, we can find the slope of the function $f$ as $m=\frac{13-5}{3-1}=4$. 
  Using the slope-intercept form of a linear function, we can find the value of $b$ by plugging in the coordinates of the point $(1,5)$ and solving for $b$. We have $5=4(1)+b$ which gives $b=1$.
  Therefore, $f(x)=4x+1$.

Question: Dreams Recalled during One Week\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|c|c|}\hline& None & 1 to 4 & 5 or more & Total \\\hline\hlineGroup X & 15 & 28 & 57 & 100 \\\hlineGroup Y & 21 & 11 & 68 & 100 \\\hlineTotal & 36 & 39 & 125 & 200 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The data in the table above were produced by a sleep researcher studying the number of dreams people recall when asked to record their dreams for one week. Group X consisted of 100 people who observed early bedtimes, and Group Y consisted of 100 people who observed later bedtimes. If a person is chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream, what is the probability that the person belonged to Group Y ?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{68}{100}$
  B: $\frac{79}{100}$
  C: $\frac{79}{164}$
  D: $\frac{164}{200}$
Response 0:
The total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream is $39+125=164$. The number of those people who belonged to Group Y is $11+68=79$. Therefore, the probability that a person chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream belonged to Group Y is:
\begin{align*}
\frac{\text{Number of people who recalled at least 1 dream in Group Y}}{\text{Total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream}} &= \frac{79}{164} \\
\end{align*}
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
The total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream is $39+125=164$. Out of these, 68 people belonged to Group Y. Therefore, the probability that a person chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream belonged to Group Y is $\frac{68}{164}$. 

Simplifying this fraction, we get:

$$\frac{68}{164}=\frac{17}{41}$$

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C) } \frac{79}{164}}$.

$$\frac{68}{164}$$

Simplifying this fraction gives:

$$\frac{68}{164} = \frac{17}{41}$$

Out of the total 200 people, 39 recalled 1 to 4 dreams and 125 recalled 5 or more dreams. So, the total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream is 39+125 = 164.

Out of these 164 people, 68 belonged to Group Y. 

Therefore, the probability that a person belonged to Group Y given that they recalled at least one dream is:

$$\frac{\text{Number of people who recalled at least 1 dream and belonged to Group Y}}{\text{Total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream}} = \frac{68}{164} = \frac{17}{41} \approx 0.415$$

Rounding to three decimal places, we get 0.415.

$$\frac{\text{number of people who recalled at least 1 dream in Group Y}}{\text{total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream}} = \frac{68}{125}$$

$$\frac{68}{125} = \frac{4\cdot 17}{5^3} = \frac{16+4}{25} = \frac{4}{5} - \frac{4}{125} = \frac{80}{100} - \frac{4}{100} = \frac{76}{100} = \frac{19}{25}$$

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C) } \frac{79}{164}}$.

  B: Median
  C: Range
  D: Standard deviation

  A: 3
  B: 8
  C: 10
  D: 27

  \begin{align*}
  3 x+3-3&=27-3 \\
  3 x &= 24
  \end{align*}
  We can then solve for $x$ by dividing both sides of the equation by 3:
  \begin{align*}
  \frac{3 x}{3} &= \frac{24}{3} \\
  x &= 8
  \end{align*}

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 55 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Keith modeled the growth over several hundred years of a tree population by estimating the number of the trees' pollen grains per square centimeter that were deposited each year within layers of a lake's sediment. He estimated there were 310 pollen grains per square centimeter the first year the grains were deposited, with a $1 \%$ annual increase in the number of grains per square centimeter thereafter. Which of the following functions models $P(t)$, the number of pollen grains per square centimeter $t$ years after the first year the grains were deposited?
Choices:
  A: $P(t)=310^{t}$
  B: $P(t)=310^{1.01 t}$
  C: $P(t)=310(0.99)^{t}$
  D: $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The initial number of pollen grains per square centimeter is 310.
  - There is a 1% increase in the number of grains per square centimeter each year.
  - We are looking for a function that models the number of pollen grains per square centimeter t years after the first year the grains were deposited.
  
We can use the formula for exponential growth to model the function:
  P(t) = P(0) * (1 + r)^t
  where P(0) is the initial number of pollen grains per square centimeter, r is the annual increase as a decimal, and t is the number of years after the first year the grains were deposited.

Using the given information:
  P(0) = 310
  r = 0.01
  
Substituting these values into the formula, we get:
  P(t) = 310 * (1 + 0.01)^t
  
Simplifying:
  P(t) = 310 * 1.01^t
  
Therefore, the answer is (D) $P(t) = 310(1.01)^{t}$. 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The initial number of pollen grains per square centimeter is 310.
  - There is a 1% annual increase in the number of pollen grains per square centimeter.
  - We are looking for a function that models the number of pollen grains per square centimeter t years after the first year the grains were deposited.
  
Process of elimination:
  - Option A does not incorporate the annual increase in pollen grains, so it cannot be the correct answer.
  - Option B has an exponent of $1.01t$ which incorporates the 1% annual increase in pollen grains, so it is a possible answer.
  - Option C has a decreasing function of $(0.99)^t$, which does not incorporate the annual increase in pollen grains, so it cannot be the correct answer.
  - Option D has an exponent of $1.01t$ which incorporates the 1% annual increase in pollen grains, so it is a possible answer.
  
Final check:
  - We can check which of the possible answers is correct by plugging in a value for t and seeing if it matches the given initial value of 310.
  - For option B, $P(1)=310^{1.01}=313.1$, which is a close approximation of $310(1.01)=313.1$, the expected value after one year.
  - For option D, $P(1)=310(1.01)^1=313.1$, which matches the expected value after one year.

  The mean of list B is $\frac{2+3+3+4+4+5}{6}=3.5$.

  The variance of list A is $\frac{(1-3.5)^2+(2-3.5)^2+(3-3.5)^2+(4-3.5)^2+(5-3.5)^2+(6-3.5)^2}{6}\approx2.92$.

Explanation: 
  The mean of list A is $\frac{1+2+3+4+5+6}{6}=3.5$.
  The mean of list B is $\frac{2+3+3+4+4+5}{6}=3.5$.
  Therefore, the means are the same.
  
  To calculate the standard deviation of list A:
  - Find the difference between each number and the mean: $1-3.5=-2.5$, $2-3.5=-1.5$, $3-3.5=-0.5$, $4-3.5=0.5$, $5-3.5=1.5$, $6-3.5=2.5$.
  - Square each difference: $(-2.5)^2=6.25$, $(-1.5)^2=2.25$, $(-0.5)^2=0.25$, $(0.5)^2=0.25$, $(1.5)^2=2.25$, $(2.5)^2=6.25$.
  - Average the squared differences: $\frac{6.25+2.25+0.25+0.25+2.25+6.25}{6}=2.5$.
  - Take the square root of the result: $\sqrt{2.5}\approx1.58$.
  Therefore, the standard deviation of list A is approximately $1.58$.
  
  To calculate the standard deviation of list B:
  - Find the difference between each number and the mean: $2-3.5=-1.5$, $3-3.5=-0.5$, $3-3.5=-0.5$, $4-3.5=0.5$, $4-3.5=0.5$, $5-3.5=1.5$.
  - Square each difference: $(-1.5)^2=2.25$, $(-0.5)^2=0.25$, $(-0.5)^2=0.25$, $(0.5)^2=0.25$, $(0.5)^2=0.25$, $(1.5)^2=2.25$.
  - Average the squared differences: $\frac{2.25+0.25+0.25+0.25+0.25+2.25}{6}=0.75$.
  - Take the square root of the result: $\sqrt{0.75}\approx0.87$.
  Therefore, the standard deviation of list B is approximately $0.87$.
  
  Since the means are different and the standard deviations are the same, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(D)}}$.

Topic: Math
Question: $$C=75 h+125$$The equation above gives the amount $C$, in dollars, an electrician charges for a job that takes $h$ hours. Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland each hired this electrician. The electrician worked 2 hours longer on Ms. Sanchez's job than on Mr. Roland's job. How much more did the electrician charge Ms. Sanchez than Mr. Roland?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 75$
  B: $\$ 125$
  C: $\$ 150$
  D: $\$ 275$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The equation $C=75h+125$ gives the amount $C$, in dollars, an electrician charges for a job that takes $h$ hours.
  Ms. Sanchez's job took 2 hours longer than Mr. Roland's job.
  We need to find the difference between the amount charged to Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland.
  
Approach:
  Let's assume Mr. Roland's job took $x$ hours.
  Then, Ms. Sanchez's job took $x+2$ hours.
  So, the amount charged to Mr. Roland is $C=75x+125$ dollars.
  And, the amount charged to Ms. Sanchez is $C=75(x+2)+125$ dollars.
  We need to find the difference between the two amounts.
  Difference = Amount charged to Ms. Sanchez - Amount charged to Mr. Roland
  
Calculation:
  Amount charged to Mr. Roland = $75x+125$
  Amount charged to Ms. Sanchez = $75(x+2)+125$
  Difference = Amount charged to Ms. Sanchez - Amount charged to Mr. Roland
  Difference = $(75(x+2)+125) - (75x+125)$
  Difference = $150$
  
Answer: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
The electrician charges $75h+125$ dollars for a job that takes $h$ hours.
Ms. Sanchez's job took 2 hours longer than Mr. Roland's job.

Let's use $h_1$ and $h_2$ to represent the number of hours the electrician worked on Ms. Sanchez's job and Mr. Roland's job, respectively.

Ms. Sanchez's job: $C = 75(h_1+2) + 125 = 75h_1 + 275$
Mr. Roland's job: $C = 75h_2 + 125$

We want to find the difference between what Ms. Sanchez paid and what Mr. Roland paid: $75h_1 + 275 - (75h_2 + 125) = 75(h_1 - h_2) + 150$

Context: Energy per Gram of Typical Macronutrients.\begin{center}.\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|}.\hline.Macronutrient & Food calories & Kilojoules \\.\hline.Protein & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.Fat & 9.0 & 37.7 \\.\hline.Carbohydrate & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.\end{tabular}.\end{center}.The table above gives the typical amounts of energy per gram, expressed in both food calories and kilojoules, of the three macronutrients in food.
Question: If the 180 food calories in a granola bar come entirely from $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate, which of the following expresses $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  C: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p-c)$
  D: $f=20+\frac{9}{4}(p+c)$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The amount of energy per gram of protein is 4.0 food calories or 16.7 kilojoules.
  The amount of energy per gram of fat is 9.0 food calories or 37.7 kilojoules.
  The amount of energy per gram of carbohydrate is 4.0 food calories or 16.7 kilojoules.
  If the 180 food calories in a granola bar come entirely from $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate, then we can write the following equation: $4p+9f+4c=180$.
Action: 
To express $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$, we need to isolate $f$ in the equation $4p+9f+4c=180$.
First, we can simplify the equation by subtracting 4p and 4c from both sides to get $9f=180-4p-4c$.
Then, we can divide both sides by 9 to get $f=\frac{180-4p-4c}{9}$.
We can further simplify this expression by factoring out a 4 from the numerator to get $f=\frac{176-4(p+c)}{9}$.
Finally, we can add 20 to both sides to get $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
Therefore, the answer is (A) $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
Response 1:

  We can use the fact that the food calories from protein, fat, and carbohydrates are proportional to the amount of protein, fat, and carbohydrates, respectively.
  
Action: 
The amount of food calories from protein is $4p$, from fat is $9f$, and from carbohydrates is $4c$. Since the granola bar contains 180 food calories, we have the equation $4p+9f+4c=180$. Solving for $f$ gives $f=\frac{20}{9}(180-4p-4c)$. Simplifying gives $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(-p-c)=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$. Therefore, the answer is (B). Answer("B").

$9f = 180 - 4p - 4c$
$f = \frac{180 - 4p - 4c}{9}$
$f = \frac{20}{9}(9) - \frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
$f = 20 - \frac{4}{9}(p+c)$

Solution:

Response 9:
Knowledge:
- The table gives the energy per gram of protein, fat, and carbohydrate in food calories and kilojoules.
- The total energy in a granola bar is 180 food calories.
- The granola bar contains protein, fat, and carbohydrate in some proportions.
- We need to express the amount of fat in terms of $p$ and $c$.

Solution:
Let $x$ be the total number of grams of protein, fat, and carbohydrate in the granola bar. We know that the total energy in the granola bar is 180 food calories. Using the table, we can express the total energy in terms of $p$, $f$, and $c$ as follows:

$4p + 9f + 4c = 180$

Simplifying this equation, we get:

$4p + 4c = 180 - 9f$

$4(p+c) = 180 - 9f$

$36 = 9f - 4(p+c)$

$9f = 4(p+c) + 36$

$f = \frac{4}{9}(p+c) + 4$

Therefore, the answer is (A) $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.

Topic: Math
Question: A painter will paint $n$ walls with the same size and shape in a building using a specific brand of paint. The painter's fee can be calculated by the expression $n K \ell h$, where $n$ is the number of walls, $K$ is a constant with units of dollars per square foot, $\ell$ is the length of each wall in feet, and $h$ is the height of each wall in feet. If the customer asks the painter to use a more expensive brand of paint, which of the factors in the expression would change?
Choices:
  A: $h$
  B: $\ell$
  C: $K$
  D: $n$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The expression for the painter's fee is $n K \ell h$.
  $n$ is the number of walls.
  $K$ is a constant with units of dollars per square foot.
  $\ell$ is the length of each wall in feet.
  $h$ is the height of each wall in feet.
Action: Answer("C")  
Explanation: 
  If the customer asks the painter to use a more expensive brand of paint, the cost per square foot, $K$, will change. The other factors in the expression, $n$, $\ell$, and $h$, are determined by the number and size of the walls and will not change. Therefore, the factor that would change is $K$.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The expression for the painter's fee is $n K \ell h$.
  The customer is asking for a more expensive brand of paint.
  The factors in the expression are $n$, $K$, $\ell$, and $h$.
Action: Answer("C")  
Explanation: If the customer asks for a more expensive brand of paint, the cost per square foot $K$ would change because it has units of dollars per square foot. The length and height of each wall, $\ell$ and $h$, respectively, would remain the same since they are properties of the walls themselves. The number of walls to be painted, $n$, would also remain the same.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 60 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: $$.\begin{aligned}.& S(P)=\frac{1}{2} P+40 \\.& D(P)=220-P.\end{aligned}.$$.The quantity of a product supplied and the quantity of the product demanded in an economic market are functions of the price of the product. The functions above are the estimated supply and demand functions for a certain product. The function $S(P)$ gives the quantity of the product supplied to the market when the price is $P$ dollars, and the function $D(P)$ gives the quantity of the product demanded by the market when the price is $P$ dollars.
Question: At what price will the quantity of the product supplied to the market equal the quantity of the product demanded by the market?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 90$
  B: $\$ 120$
  C: $\$ 133$
  D: $\$ 155$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The quantity of the product supplied to the market will equal the quantity of the product demanded by the market when the price is such that $S(P) = D(P)$.
  $S(P)=\frac{1}{2} P+40$ gives the quantity of the product supplied to the market when the price is $P$ dollars.
  $D(P)=220-P$ gives the quantity of the product demanded by the market when the price is $P$ dollars.
Action: 
  Set $S(P) = D(P)$ and solve for $P$:
  $$\frac{1}{2} P+40 = 220-P$$
  $$\frac{3}{2} P = 180$$
  $$P = 120$$
  Answer: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The quantity of the product supplied equals the quantity of the product demanded in the market when $S(P) = D(P)$.
  $S(P)=\frac{1}{2} P+40$ is the estimated supply function.
  $D(P)=220-P$ is the estimated demand function.

Action: 
  Equating the supply and demand functions we have:
  $$\frac{1}{2} P+40 = 220-P$$
  Solving for $P$:
  $$\frac{3}{2} P = 180$$
  $$P = 120$$
  Answer: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The quantity of the product supplied to the market equals the quantity of the product demanded by the market at the equilibrium price.
  To find the equilibrium price, we need to find the price $P$ that makes $S(P)=D(P)$.
Action: 
Substitute $S(P)$ and $D(P)$ with their respective expressions and solve for $P$:
$$\frac{1}{2}P+40=220-P$$
$$\frac{1}{2}P+P=220-40$$
$$\frac{3}{2}P=180$$
$$P=120$$
Answer: Answer("B")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  The quantity of the product supplied equals the quantity of the product demanded when $S(P)=D(P)$.
  $S(P)=\frac{1}{2}P+40$ is the supply function.
  $D(P)=220-P$ is the demand function.
Action: 
  Equate the supply and demand functions to find the price that will make the quantity supplied equal to the quantity demanded:
  $$\begin{aligned}
  S(P)&=D(P)\\
  \frac{1}{2}P+40&=220-P\\
  \frac{3}{2}P&=180\\
  P&=120
  \end{aligned}$$
  Answer: Answer("B")

Knowledge: The quantity of the product supplied and the quantity of the product demanded in an economic market are equal at the market equilibrium price, which is the price where the supply and demand functions intersect.
To find the market equilibrium price, we need to find the value of $P$ that satisfies the equation $S(P)=D(P)$.

Action: 
We have:
$$S(P)=\frac{1}{2} P+40$$
$$D(P)=220-P$$
Setting $S(P)=D(P)$, we get:
$$\frac{1}{2} P+40=220-P$$
Simplifying and solving for $P$, we get:
$$\frac{3}{2} P=180$$
$$P=120$$
Therefore, the market equilibrium price is $\$120$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 61 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $\frac{5}{x}=\frac{15}{x+20}$, what is the value of $\frac{x}{5} ?$
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 5
  C: 2
  D: $\frac{1}{2}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  We can solve the equation $\frac{5}{x}=\frac{15}{x+20}$ by cross-multiplying and simplifying.
  If we have $\frac{5}{x}=\frac{15}{x+20}$, then we can cross-multiply to get $5(x+20)=15x$.
  Solving for $x$, we have $x=20$.
  We can then find the value of $\frac{x}{5}$ by dividing $x$ by $5$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  To solve the equation $\frac{a}{b}=\frac{c}{d}$, where $b$ and $d$ are not zero, we can cross-multiply and get $ad=bc$.
  
Action: 
  Cross-multiplying the given equation, we have $5(x+20)=15x$. Expanding the left-hand side, we get $5x+100=15x$. Subtracting $5x$ from both sides, we get $100=10x$. Dividing both sides by $10$, we get $x=10$. Therefore, $\frac{x}{5}=2$. 
  Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  We can solve the equation $\frac{5}{x}=\frac{15}{x+20}$ by cross multiplying and solving for $x$. 
  Cross multiplying gives us $5(x+20)=15x$, which simplifies to $x=20$.
Action: 
  We can substitute $x=20$ into the expression $\frac{x}{5}$ to get $\frac{20}{5}=4$.
  Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(A)}\ 10}$.
Response 3:
Knowledge:

  We can cross-multiply to solve for the variable in a proportion.
  Cross-multiplying means multiplying the numerator of one fraction by the denominator of the other fraction.
  If two fractions are equal, then their reciprocals are also equal.
  
Solution:

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 62 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$$In the equation above, $k$ is a constant. If $x=9$, what is the value of $k$ ?
Choices:

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 63 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: $$.a=1,052+1.08 t.$$.The speed of a sound wave in air depends on the air temperature. The formula above shows the relationship between $a$, the speed of a sound wave, in feet per second, and $t$, the air temperature, in degrees Fahrenheit $\left({ }^{\circ} \mathrm{F}\right)$.
Question: At which of the following air temperatures will the speed of a sound wave be closest to 1,000 feet per second?
Choices:
  A: $-46^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
  B: $-48^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
  C: $-49^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
  D: $-50^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The formula for the speed of sound in air at a temperature of $t$ degrees Fahrenheit is given by $a=1,052+1.08 t$ feet per second.
  We want to find the temperature at which the speed of sound is closest to 1,000 feet per second.
  
Action: 
  We can solve this problem by finding the value of $t$ that makes $a$ closest to 1,000 feet per second. 
  We can start by finding the value of $t$ that makes $a$ exactly 1,000 feet per second:
  \begin{aligned} 1,000 &=1,052+1.08 t \\ -52 &=1.08 t \\ t &\approx-48.15 \end{aligned}
  This means that at a temperature of $-48.15^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$, the speed of sound is exactly 1,000 feet per second. 
  Since we are looking for the temperature at which the speed of sound is closest to 1,000 feet per second, we need to find the temperature that is closest to $-48.15^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$ from the given choices. 
  The answer is the temperature that has the smallest absolute difference from $-48.15^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$. 
  Calculating the absolute differences for each choice: 
  - $|-46-(-48.15)|=2.15$
  - $|-48-(-48.15)|=0.15$
  - $|-49-(-48.15)|=0.85$
  - $|-50-(-48.15)|=1.85$
  The smallest absolute difference is for choice B, which is $-48^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$. 
  Therefore, the answer is B. Answer("B")

Question: $$2 a x-15=3(x+5)+5(x-1)$$In the equation above, $a$ is a constant. If no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, what is the value of $a$ ?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 2
  C: 4
  D: 8
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To solve the equation, we need to simplify and combine like terms. This will give us an equation in the form of $bx + c = 0$, where $b$ and $c$ are constants. If no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, then the equation has no solutions. This means that the discriminant of the equation is negative.
Action: 
We start by simplifying the equation:
$$2ax - 15 = 3x + 15 + 5x - 5$$
Simplifying further:
$$2ax - 15 = 8x + 10$$
$$2ax - 8x = 25$$
$$2x(a-4) = 25$$
$$x = \frac{25}{2(a-4)}$$
Since there is no value of $x$ that satisfies the equation, the denominator must be equal to zero. Therefore, we have:
$$a-4 = 0$$
$$a = 4$$

Question: The function $f$ is defined by $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$. The graph of $f$ in the $x y$-plane is a parabola. Which of the following intervals contains the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: $-4<x<-3$
  B: $-3<x<1$
  C: $1<x<3$
  D: $3<x<4$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The vertex of a parabola in the form $f(x) = a(x-h)^2+k$ is located at $(h,k)$.
  The vertex of a parabola in the form $f(x) = ax^2+bx+c$ is located at $(-\frac{b}{2a}, f(-\frac{b}{2a}))$.

Action: 
  We can expand $f(x)$ and get $f(x) = x^2 + 4x + 3$. 
  The $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of $f$ is $-\frac{b}{2a} = -\frac{4}{2(1)} = -2$.
  Therefore, the answer is an interval that contains $-2$.
  A: $-4 < -2 < -3$, so $-2$ is in this interval.
  B: $-3 < -2 < 1$, so $-2$ is in this interval.
  C: $1 < -2 < 3$, so $-2$ is not in this interval.
  D: $3 < -2 < 4$, so $-2$ is not in this interval.

  Therefore, the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of $f$ is in the interval $-3<x<1$.

Question: $$\frac{2}{3}(9 x-6)-4=9 x-6$$Based on the equation above, what is the value of $3 x-2$ ?
Choices:
  A: -4
  B: $-\frac{4}{5}$
  C: $-\frac{2}{3}$
  D: 4
Response 0:
$$\frac{2}{3}(9x-6)-4=9x-6$$
$$6x-4-4=9x-6$$
$$6x-8=9x-6$$
$$-3x=2$$
$$x=-\frac{2}{3}$$
$$3x-2=3\left(-\frac{2}{3}\right)-2=-2-2=\boxed{\textbf{(D) }4}$$

Action: Answer("D")

Knowledge:

  Combining like terms on the left side of the equation gives us $6x-4-4=9x-6$
  Simplifying the equation gives us $6x-8=9x-6$
  Isolating the variable gives us $x=2$

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 69 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$Clayton will mix $x$ milliliters of a $10 \%$ by mass saline solution with $y$ milliliters of a $20 \%$ by mass saline solution in order to create an $18 \%$ by mass saline solution. The equation above represents this situation. If Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution, how many milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution must he use?
Choices:
  A: 5
  B: 25
  C: 50
  D: 100
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's multiply both sides of the equation by 100 to get rid of the decimals.
  $$10x+20y=18(x+y)$$
  We can distribute the $18$ on the right side of the equation.
  $$10x+20y=18x+18y$$
  We can simplify by subtracting $10x$ and $18y$ from both sides of the equation.
  $$2y=8x$$
  $$y=4x$$
  We also know that Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ saline solution, so $y=100$.
Action: 
  Substituting $y=100$ into $y=4x$, we get $100=4x$. Solving for $x$, we get $x=25$.
  Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The given equation represents the amount of salt in the two solutions before and after the mixture.
  We can solve for one variable in terms of the other to find the ratio of the two solutions needed to make the desired mixture.
  We can then use the information about one of the solutions to find the amount of the other solution needed.
Action: 
  First, we can simplify the given equation by multiplying both sides by 100 to get rid of the decimals:
  $$10x+20y=18(x+y)$$
  Then, we can distribute the 18 on the right-hand side:
  $$10x+20y=18x+18y$$
  Next, we can isolate one of the variables, say $x$, on one side:
  $$2y=8x$$
  $$x=\frac{1}{4}y$$
  This means that for every 4 milliliters of the $20 \%$ solution, we need 1 milliliter of the $10 \%$ solution.
  Since Clayton is using 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ solution, he needs:
  $$\frac{1}{4} \cdot 100 = 25$$
  milliliters of the $10 \%$ solution.
  Therefore, the answer is (B) 25.
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The equation $$0.10x+0.20y=0.18(x+y)$$ can be simplified to $$0.02x=0.02y,$$ which can be further simplified to $$x=y.$$

  Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution.
Action: 
  Since $x=y$, and Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution, we have $$x+100=total \ amount \ of \ solution.$$ 
  Also, we know that the final solution is $18 \%$ saline. Therefore, we can write the following equation: $$0.10x+0.20(100)=0.18(x+100).$$
  Solving for $x$, we get $$x=50.$$ 
  Thus, Clayton must use 50 milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution. 
  Action: Answer("C")

Knowledge:

  D: 72

Question: In planning maintenance for a city's infrastructure, a civil engineer estimates that, starting from the present, the population of the city will decrease by 10 percent every 20 years. If the present population of the city is 50,000, which of the following expressions represents the engineer's estimate of the population of the city $t$ years from now?
Choices:
  A: $50,000(0.1)^{20 t}$
  B: $50,000(0.1)^{\frac{t}{20}}$
  C: $50,000(0.9)^{20 t}$
  D: $50,000(0.9)^{\frac{t}{20}}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If the population of a city decreases by $r$ percent every $n$ years, then the new population $P$ after $t$ years is given by the formula $P = P_0(1 - \frac{r}{100})^{\frac{t}{n}}$, where $P_0$ is the initial population.
  A: This expression is incorrect because it uses the decay factor of 0.1, which represents a decrease of 10% every year, not every 20 years.
  B: This expression is correct because it uses the decay factor of 0.1, which represents a decrease of 10% every 20 years, and raises it to the power of $\frac{t}{20}$ to represent the number of 20-year periods that have passed.
  C: This expression is incorrect because it uses the wrong decay factor of 0.9, which represents a decrease of 90% every 20 years.
  D: This expression is incorrect because it uses the wrong decay factor of 0.9, which represents a decrease of 90% every 20 years, and raises it to the power of $\frac{t}{20}$ instead of $\frac{-t}{20}$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The population of the city is decreasing by 10 percent every 20 years.
  The present population of the city is 50,000.
  
To solve this problem, we can use the formula: 

$P(t) = P_0(1-r)^{\frac{t}{T}}$

where:
  P(t) is the population after t years
  P_0 is the initial population
  r is the rate of decrease (as a decimal)
  T is the time period over which the rate applies (in years)
  
Using the given information, we can plug in the values to the formula and simplify.

Action: Answer("D") 

The correct expression is: $50,000(0.9)^{\frac{t}{20}}$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 76 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A rectangle was altered by increasing its length by 10 percent and decreasing its width by $p$ percent. If these alterations decreased the area of the rectangle by 12 percent, what is the value of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: 12
  B: 15
  C: 20
  D: 22
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let $l$ and $w$ be the original length and width of the rectangle, respectively. Then the area of the rectangle is $lw$. 
  The new length is $1.1l$ (a 10% increase) and the new width is $(1-\frac{p}{100})w$ (a $p$% decrease). 
  The new area is $(1-0.12)lw=0.88lw$ (a 12% decrease). 
  We want to solve for $p$.
  
Solution:
  The new area is $(1-0.12)lw=0.88lw$. 
  The new length is $1.1l$ and the new width is $(1-\frac{p}{100})w$. 
  So we have $(1.1l)(1-\frac{p}{100})w=0.88lw$. 
  Simplifying gives $1.1-\frac{1.1p}{100}-\frac{12}{100}=0.88$. 
  Solving for $p$ gives $\frac{22}{11}=1.1p$, which implies $p=\boxed{\textbf{(D) }22}$. 

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let L be the original length of the rectangle and W be the original width of the rectangle.
  The original area of the rectangle is A = L x W.
  After the alterations, the new length is 1.1L and the new width is (1-p/100)W.
  The new area of the rectangle is 0.88A (since the area decreased by 12 percent).
  We can set up an equation: (1.1L)(1-p/100)W = 0.88A = 0.88LW.
  We can simplify this equation to: 1.1(1-p/100) = 0.88.
  We can solve for p using algebraic manipulation.

  Therefore, $p = 100 - \frac{100}{1.1} \times 0.12 \approx 20.0$.

  $1-\frac{p}{100} = \frac{0.88}{1.10}$
  $1-\frac{p}{100} = 0.8$
  $\frac{p}{100} = 0.2$
  $p = 20$

  Therefore, 1.1L * (1-p/100)W = 0.9856A.

Knowledge:
  Let the original length and width of the rectangle be $l$ and $w$, respectively. Then, the original area of the rectangle is $lw$.
  If we increase the length of the rectangle by 10 percent, its new length becomes $1.1l$.
  If we decrease the width of the rectangle by $p$ percent, its new width becomes $(100-p)\%$ of the original width, or $\frac{(100-p)}{100}w$.
