### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 83 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|}\hline\multicolumn{3}{|c|}{Townsend Realty Group Investments} \\\hlineProperty address & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Purchase price } \\ \text { (dollars) }\end{array}$ & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Monthly rental } \\ \text { price } \\ \text { (dollars) }\end{array}$ \\\hlineClearwater Lane & 128,000 & 950 \\\hlineDriftwood Drive & 176,000 & 1,310 \\\hlineEdgemont Street & 70,000 & 515 \\\hlineGlenview Street & 140,000 & 1,040 \\\hlineHamilton Circle & 450,000 & 3,365 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The Townsend Realty Group invested in the five different properties listed in the table above. The table shows the amount, in dollars, the company paid for each property and the corresponding monthly rental price, in dollars, the company charges for the property at each of the five locations. 23The relationship between the monthly rental price $r$, in dollars, and the property's purchase price $p$, in thousands of dollars, can be represented by a linear function. Which of the following functions represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $r(p)=2.5 p-870$
  B: $r(p)=5 p+165$
  C: $r(p)=6.5 p+440$
  D: $r(p)=7.5 p-10$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To find the linear function that represents the relationship between two variables, we need to use the formula for a line: $y = mx + b$, where $y$ is the dependent variable, $x$ is the independent variable, $m$ is the slope of the line, and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  To find the slope of the line, we use the formula: $m = \frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}$, where $\Delta y$ is the change in the dependent variable and $\Delta x$ is the change in the independent variable.
  In this case, the independent variable is the purchase price $p$, and the dependent variable is the monthly rental price $r$.
  We can use any two points from the table to find the slope. For example, we can use the points $(128, 950)$ and $(176, 1310)$ to find the slope: $m = \frac{1310-950}{176-128} = \frac{360}{48} = 7.5$.
  To find the y-intercept, we can use any point on the line and the slope. For example, we can use the point $(128, 950)$ and the slope $m = 7.5$ to find the y-intercept: $950 = 7.5 \cdot 128 + b$, which gives $b = -10$.
  Therefore, the linear function that represents the relationship between the monthly rental price $r$ and the property's purchase price $p$ is $r(p) = 7.5p - 10$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:

- For Driftwood Drive: $p=176$ and $r=1310$

$m=\dfrac{\text{change in r}}{\text{change in p}}=\dfrac{1310-950}{176-128}=6.4$

$r-r_1=m(p-p_1)$, where $(p_1,r_1)$ is any point on the line.

We can use the point $(128,950)$:
$r-950=6.4(p-128)$
$r=6.4p-870.4$

We can simplify this equation to match the answer choices:
$r(p)=6.4p-870.4=6.4p-870+440-10$

Question: To make a bakery's signature chocolate muffins, a baker needs 2.5 ounces of chocolate for each muffin. How many pounds of chocolate are needed to make 48 signature chocolate muffins?( 1 pound $=16$ ounces)
Choices:
  A: 7.5
  B: 10
  C: 50.5
  D: 120
Response 0:
Knowledge:
- 1 pound = 16 ounces
- The baker needs 2.5 ounces of chocolate for each muffin
- The baker wants to make 48 muffins

Calculation:
- To find out how many ounces of chocolate the baker needs in total, we multiply the amount of chocolate needed for each muffin by the number of muffins: 2.5 ounces/muffin * 48 muffins = 120 ounces
- To convert ounces to pounds, we divide by 16: 120 ounces / 16 ounces/pound = 7.5 pounds

  D: 1,400 meters

Question: The first year Eleanor organized a fund-raising event, she invited 30 people. For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year. If $f(n)$ is the number of people invited to the fund-raiser $n$ years after Eleanor began organizing the event, which of the following statements best describes the function $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: The function $f$ is a decreasing linear function.
  B: The function $f$ is an increasing linear function.
  C: The function $f$ is a decreasing exponential function.
  D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  In the first year, Eleanor invited 30 people.
  For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year.
  Let's use $n$ to represent the number of years after Eleanor began organizing the event.
  Therefore, we can represent the number of people invited by Eleanor in year $n$ as $f(n)$.
  In the first year, $n=1$, and $f(1)=30$.
  In the second year, $n=2$, and $f(2)=2 \times f(1)=2 \times 30=60$.
  In the third year, $n=3$, and $f(3)=2 \times f(2)=2 \times 60=120$.
  Similarly, we can find that $f(4)=240$, $f(5)=480$.
  We can see that the function $f$ is increasing and exponential since the number of people invited is doubling each year.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 89 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Survey Results\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|}\hlineAnswer & Percent \\\hlineNever & $31.3 \%$ \\\hlineRarely & $24.3 \%$ \\\hlineOften & $13.5 \%$ \\\hlineAlways & $30.9 \%$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows the results of a survey in which tablet users were asked how often they would watch video advertisements in order to access streaming content for free. Based on the table, which of the following is closest to the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never"?
Choices:
  A: 0.31
  B: 0.38
  C: 0.45
  D: 0.69
Response 0:
Let's first focus on the relevant part of the table: 

\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|}\hlineAnswer & Percent \\\hlineNever & $31.3 \%$ \\\hline ... \\\hlineAlways & $30.9 \%$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}

The question asks for the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never". This is a conditional probability, and we can use the formula:

$P(\text{Always} \mid \text{not Never}) = \dfrac{P(\text{Always and not Never})}{P(\text{not Never})}$

We can find the numerator by multiplying the percentages for "Always" and "not Never" (which means the user answered "Rarely," "Often," or "Always"):

$P(\text{Always and not Never}) = 0.309 \times (1-0.313) = 0.212617$

We can find the denominator by subtracting the percentage for "Never" from 100%:

$P(\text{not Never}) = 1 - 0.313 = 0.687$

Now we can use the formula to find the conditional probability:

$P(\text{Always} \mid \text{not Never}) = \dfrac{P(\text{Always and not Never})}{P(\text{not Never})} \approx \boxed{\textbf{(B) }0.38}$
Response 1:
Let's use Bayes' theorem to compute the probability of a tablet user answering "Always" given they did not answer "Never". Let A be the event that a tablet user answered "Always" and N be the event that a tablet user answered "Never". Then, we want to find P(A|not N). We can compute this as follows:

P(A|not N) = P(not N|A) * P(A) / P(not N)

We can compute each of these probabilities using the information given in the table:

P(A) = 0.309
P(N) = 0.313
P(not N) = 1 - P(N) = 0.687
P(not N|A) = 1 - P(N|A) = 1 - 0 = 1 (since if someone answered "Always", they did not answer "Never")

Now we can substitute these values into the equation to get:

P(A|not N) = (1 * 0.309) / 0.687 = 0.38 (rounded to two decimal places)

Therefore, the closest choice to the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never" is B: 0.38. 

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:

We can use Bayes' theorem: $$P(A|B) = \frac{P(B|A)P(A)}{P(B)},$$ where $P(B|A)$ is the probability that a tablet user did not answer "Never," given that the tablet user answered "Always," $P(A)$ is the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," and $P(B)$ is the probability that a tablet user did not answer "Never." 

From the table, we see that $P(A) = 0.309$ and $P(B) = 1 - 0.313 = 0.687.$ To find $P(B|A),$ we note that all of the tablet users who answered "Always" also did not answer "Never," so $P(B|A) = 1.$ 

Therefore, $$P(A|B) = \frac{P(B|A)P(A)}{P(B)} = \frac{1 \cdot 0.309}{0.687} \approx 0.45.$$

  P(Always | Not Never)  0.45
Answer: "C"
Response 9:
Knowledge: 
  The table shows the percentage of respondents who answered "Never", "Rarely", "Often", and "Always".
  The question asks for the probability of answering "Always" given that the respondent did not answer "Never". This means we need to calculate the probability of answering "Always" among those who did not answer "Never".
  We can calculate this probability using conditional probability: P(Always | Not Never) = P(Always and Not Never) / P(Not Never)
  P(Not Never) = 100% - P(Never)
  We can use the values in the table to calculate the probabilities.
  
Action: 
  P(Not Never) = 100% - 31.3% = 68.7%
  P(Always and Not Never) = 30.9%
  P(Always | Not Never) = P(Always and Not Never) / P(Not Never) = 30.9% / 68.7% = 0.449
  The closest choice to 0.449 is C: 0.45

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& 2 x-3 y=-14 \\& 3 x-2 y=-6\end{aligned}$$If $(x, y)$ is a solution to the system of equations above, what is the value of $x-y$ ?
Choices:
  A: -20
  B: $\quad-8$
  C: -4
  D: 8
Response 0:
Knowledge: To solve the system of equations, we can use the elimination method. We can multiply the first equation by 2 and the second equation by 3, then subtract the second equation from the first to eliminate $y$ and solve for $x$. Then we can substitute the value of $x$ into one of the equations to solve for $y$. Finally, we can calculate $x-y$ using the values of $x$ and $y$ we found.
Action: 
Multiplying the first equation by 2 and the second equation by 3, we get:
$$\begin{aligned}& 4 x-6 y=-28 \\& 9 x-6 y=-18\end{aligned}$$
Subtracting the second equation from the first, we get:
$$\begin{aligned} -5x &= -10 \\ x &= 2 \end{aligned}$$
Substituting $x=2$ into the first equation, we get:
$$\begin{aligned} 2(2)-3y &= -14 \\ -3y &= -18 \\ y &= 6 \end{aligned}$$
Therefore, $(x,y) = (2,6)$, and $x-y = -4$. 

Answer: Answer("C")

$$\begin{aligned}&\begin{aligned}2 x-3 y&=-14\\2(2 x-3 y)&=2(-14)\end{aligned}\\&\qquad\quad\Rightarrow\begin{aligned}4 x-6 y&=-28\end{aligned}\end{aligned}$$

$$2\left(-\frac{46}{13}\right)-3 y=-14 \Rightarrow y=\frac{20}{13}$$

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: Jennifer bought a box of Crunchy Grain cereal. The nutrition facts on the box state that a serving size of the cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories, 50 of which are calories from fat. In addition, each serving of the cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
Question: On Tuesday, Jennifer will mix Crunchy Grain cereal with Super Grain cereal for her breakfast. Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup. If the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270, how much Super Grain cereal is in one cup of the mixture?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{1}{8} \operatorname{cup}$
  B: $\frac{1}{4} \operatorname{cup}$
  C: $\frac{1}{3} \operatorname{cup}$
  D: $\frac{1}{2} \operatorname{cup}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  * A serving size of Crunchy Grain cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories, 50 of which are from fat.
  * Each serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
  * Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup.
  * The total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270.
  
Calculations:
  Let's assume that Jennifer mixes $x$ cups of Super Grain cereal with $y$ cups of Crunchy Grain cereal. Then, we can set up the following equations to represent the total calories and the total volume of the mixture:
  * Total calories: $240x + 210y = 270$, since each cup of Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories and each $\frac{3}{4}$ cup of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 210 calories.
  * Total volume: $x + y = 1$, since Jennifer is mixing one cup of cereal in total.
  
  We can solve the second equation for $y$ to get $y = 1 - x$. Substituting this expression for $y$ in the first equation, we get:
  $$240x + 210(1 - x) = 270$$
  Simplifying and solving for $x$, we get $x = \frac{1}{3}$.
  
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  1 cup of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 280 calories ($\frac{3}{4}$ cup provides 210 calories).
  Each serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
  Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup.
  The total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270.
Action:

$$240x + 210 = 270$$
Solving for $x$:
$$240x = 60$$
$$x = \frac{60}{240} = \frac{1}{4}$$
So, Jennifer mixes $\frac{1}{4}$ cup of Super Grain cereal with $\frac{3}{4}$ cup of Crunchy Grain cereal. 
To check the answer, we can calculate the total number of calories in one cup of the mixture:
$$240 \cdot \frac{1}{4} + 280 \cdot \frac{3}{4} = 60 + 210 = 270$$
Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ \frac{1}{4} \operatorname{cup}}$.

  - Jennifer's mixture contains Crunchy Grain cereal and Super Grain cereal.
  - Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup.
  - The total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270.
Action: 
Let's assume that Jennifer mixes $x$ cups of Super Grain cereal with $(1 - x)$ cups of Crunchy Grain cereal to make one cup of the mixture. 
The total number of calories in the mixture is the sum of the calories from each type of cereal. 
From the information given, we know that the total number of calories in one cup of the mixture is 270. 
So we can write the following equation: 

$(240x) + \left(210 \cdot \frac{3}{4} \cdot (1-x)\right) = 270$

Simplifying this equation, we get:

$240x + 157.5 - 157.5x = 270$

$82.5x = 112.5$

$x = \frac{112.5}{82.5} \approx 1.36$

Since we assumed that Jennifer mixes $x$ cups of Super Grain cereal with $(1 - x)$ cups of Crunchy Grain cereal, and $x$ cannot be greater than 1, this solution is not possible. 

Therefore, the answer must be less than $\frac{3}{4}$ cup (the amount of Crunchy Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture). 

To find the answer, we can set up a new equation based on the total number of calories from the Super Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture:

$(240x) = (270 - 210 \cdot \frac{3}{4} \cdot (1-x))$

Simplifying this equation, we get:

$240x = 127.5 - 157.5x$

$397.5x = 127.5$

$x = \frac{127.5}{397.5} \approx 0.32$

So, the amount of Super Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture is approximately $0.32$ cups. 

Rounding to the nearest quarter cup, we get $\frac{1}{3}$ cup. 

Therefore, the answer is (C) $\frac{1}{3} \operatorname{cup}$.

Topic: Math
Question: $$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$The equation above gives the height $h$, in feet, of a ball $t$ seconds after it is thrown straight up with an initial speed of $v$ feet per second from a height of $k$ feet. Which of the following gives $v$ in terms of $h, t$, and $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: $v=h+k-16 t$
  B: $v=\frac{h-k+16}{t}$
  C: $v=\frac{h+k}{t}-16 t$
  D: $v=\frac{h-k}{t}+16 t$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The given equation is a quadratic function in $t$ with a leading coefficient of $-16$. 
  The coefficient of $t$ is the initial speed $v$.
  The constant term is the initial height $k$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The given equation is a form of the kinematic equation for the vertical motion of an object thrown upwards from the ground.
  The initial velocity $v$ is the coefficient of $t$ in the equation.
  $h$, $t$, $v$, and $k$ represent height, time, initial velocity, and initial height respectively.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The given equation is a quadratic function in $t$.
  The coefficient of $t^2$ is negative, indicating that the function has a maximum value.
  The initial velocity $v$ is the coefficient of $t$ in the equation.
  The value of $h$ when $t=0$ is $k$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
The given equation is a quadratic equation in standard form. It gives the height of a ball at any time $t$ after it is thrown vertically upward with an initial velocity $v$ from a height $k$. When the ball reaches its maximum height, its velocity becomes zero. Therefore, the initial velocity $v$ can be found by using the maximum height $h$ and the time $t$ it takes to reach that height. 

To find the time it takes to reach the maximum height, we can use the fact that at the maximum height, the velocity of the ball is zero. Therefore, we can set the velocity equation equal to zero and solve for $t$. 

Action: 
$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$

At maximum height, $v=0$.

$0=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$

$v t=16 t^{2}-k$

$v=16 t-\frac{k}{t}$

Multiplying both sides of the equation by $\frac{t}{t}$, we get:

$v=\frac{16 t^{2}-k}{t}$

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ v=\frac{h-k+16}{t}}$.
Response 4:
Knowledge:

To solve for $v$, we need to isolate $v$ on one side of the equation. 

Action: 
Rearranging the given equation, we get: 
$$
v = \frac{h-k}{t} + 16t
$$
Therefore, the answer is (D).
Response 5:
Knowledge:
We can solve for $v$ by rearranging the given equation. If we differentiate $h$ with respect to $t$, we get $v-32t$, which means $v=32t+h$ when the ball hits the ground. However, in this problem, the ball is not hitting the ground, so we need to add $+k$ to the equation. Therefore, $v=32t+h+k$.

Response 8:
Knowledge: 
The given equation is a quadratic equation that models the height of a ball thrown straight up in the air. The coefficient of $t^2$ is negative, which means that the parabolic shape of the graph is downward facing. The initial height of the ball is $k$ and the initial velocity is $v$. 

To find $v$, we need to isolate the term with $v$ on one side of the equation.

Action:

  $$v t = -16 t^{2}+h-k$$
  Dividing both sides by $t$, we get:
  $$v = -16 t+\frac{h-k}{t}$$
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  $$v = -16 t+\frac{h}{t}-\frac{k}{t}$$

Question: $$-2 x+3 y=6$$In the $x y$-plane, the graph of which of the following equations is perpendicular to the graph of the equation above?

  A: $3 x+2 y=6$
  B: $3 x+4 y=6$
  C: $2 x+4 y=6$
  D: $2 x+6 y=3$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Two lines are perpendicular if and only if the product of their slopes is -1.
  The slope-intercept form of a line is $y = mx + b$, where $m$ is the slope of the line.
  The slope of a line in the standard form $Ax + By = C$ is $-\frac{A}{B}$.
  
Action: 
  First, we need to write the given equation in slope-intercept form.
  $$-2x + 3y = 6 \Rightarrow 3y = 2x + 6 \Rightarrow y = \frac{2}{3}x + 2$$
  The slope of this line is $\frac{2}{3}$.
  To be perpendicular, the slope of the other line must be $-\frac{3}{2}$.
  A: The slope of this line is $-\frac{3}{2}$, so it is perpendicular to the given line. 
  B: The slope of this line is $-\frac{3}{4}$, so it is not perpendicular to the given line.
  C: The slope of this line is $-\frac{1}{2}$, so it is not perpendicular to the given line.
  D: The slope of this line is $-\frac{1}{3}$, so it is not perpendicular to the given line.
  
Therefore, the answer is A: $3x + 2y = 6$. Answer("A")

Question: $$\frac{x}{x-3}=\frac{2 x}{2}$$Which of the following represents all the possible values of $x$ that satisfy the equation above?
Choices:
  A: 0 and 2
  B: 0 and 4
  C: -4 and 4
  D: 4
Response 0:
Knowledge:
To solve the equation, we can cross-multiply and simplify to get:
$$2(x-3)=x \Rightarrow 2x-6=x \Rightarrow x=6$$
Therefore, $x=6$ is the only solution that satisfies the equation.
A: Neither 0 nor 2 satisfy the equation.
B: Neither 0 nor 4 satisfy the equation.
C: Neither -4 nor 4 satisfy the equation.
D: 4 does not satisfy the equation.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

  $$x(x-3)=x(1)$$
  $$x^2-3x=x$$
  $$x^2-4x=0$$
  $$x(x-4)=0$$
  $$x=0 \text{ or } x=4$$

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 99 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$In the system of equations above, $k$ is a constant and $x$ and $y$ are variables. For what value of $k$ will the system of equations have no solution?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{12}{5}$
  B: $\frac{16}{7}$
  C: $-\frac{16}{7}$
  D: $-\frac{12}{5}$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  For a system of two linear equations in two variables $x$ and $y$, $ax+by=c$ and $dx+ey=f$, it has no solution if and only if the lines corresponding to the equations are parallel and non-intersecting. 
  The slopes of the lines are $-\frac{a}{b}$ and $-\frac{d}{e}$, respectively.
  If $-\frac{a}{b}=-\frac{d}{e}$ and $c\ne f$, then the lines are parallel and non-intersecting.
  
Action: 
  Rewrite the given system of equations in the form of $ax+by=c$ and $dx+ey=f$:
  $$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \quad \Rightarrow \quad 3y=kx-4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7 \quad \Rightarrow \quad 5y=4x-7 \quad \Rightarrow \quad y=\frac{4}{5}x-\frac{7}{5}\end{aligned}$$
  The slopes of the lines are $-\frac{3}{k}$ and $-\frac{4}{5}$, respectively.
  The lines are parallel and non-intersecting if $-\frac{3}{k}=-\frac{4}{5}$ and $-4\ne -\frac{7}{5}$.
  Solving $-\frac{3}{k}=-\frac{4}{5}$ gives $k=\frac{12}{5}$.
  Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(A) }\frac{12}{5}}$.
Response 1:
Knowledge: To determine if the system of equations has no solution, we can use the determinant of the coefficient matrix. If the determinant is zero, then there is no unique solution. 
For a system of equations in the form of $$\begin{aligned}& a x+b y=c \\& d x+e y=f\end{aligned}$$ the determinant of the coefficient matrix is given by $ae-bd$.

Action: 
The determinant of the coefficient matrix is $k(-5)-(-3)(4)= -5k+12$. 
The system has no solution if the determinant is zero. 
So we need to solve the equation $-5k+12=0$ to find the value of $k$ that makes the determinant zero.
$$\begin{aligned}-5k+12&=0\\-5k&=-12\\k&=\frac{12}{5}\end{aligned}$$
Therefore, the value of $k$ that makes the system of equations have no solution is $\frac{12}{5}$. 
Answer: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  A system of linear equations has no solution if the equations are inconsistent, that is, they do not share a common solution.
  Two linear equations in two variables can be solved using the elimination method, which involves adding or subtracting one equation from the other to eliminate one of the variables.
  If the coefficients of one of the variables are proportional in the two equations, then eliminating that variable will result in an equation with no variables, which can be used to determine the value of the other variable.
  To check whether the system has no solution, we can use the value of the variable obtained and substitute it into the other equation to see if it is satisfied.

Action: 
We can eliminate $y$ by multiplying the first equation by $5$ and the second equation by $3$ and adding them:
$$\begin{aligned}5(kx-3y)&=20 \\ 3(4x-5y)&=21\end{aligned}$$
Simplifying each equation gives:
$$\begin{aligned}5kx-15y&=20 \\ 12x-15y&=21\end{aligned}$$

$$5kx-12x=20-21$$
Simplifying gives:
$$x=-\frac{1}{7k-4}$$

$$4\left(-\frac{1}{7k-4}\right)-5y=7$$
Simplifying gives:
$$-\frac{4}{7k-4}-5y=7$$
Multiplying both sides by $7k-4$ gives:
$$-4-5y(7k-4)=7(7k-4)$$
Simplifying gives:
$$-35ky+28y=45k-21$$
Factoring out $y$ gives:
$$y(-35k+28)=45k-21$$
If the system has no solution, then the equations are inconsistent, which means that the left-hand side of the last equation is zero, but the right-hand side is not. Therefore, we need to find the value of $k$ that makes the left-hand side zero:
$$-35k+28=0$$
Solving for $k$ gives:
$$k=\frac{28}{35}=\frac{4}{5}$$

Question: If $\frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2}$, what is the value of $\frac{b}{a} ?$
Choices:
  A: $\frac{1}{8}$
  B: $\frac{1}{4}$
  C: 2
  D: 4
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To solve for $\frac{b}{a}$, we can manipulate the given equation as follows:
  $$
  \frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2} \quad \Rightarrow \quad
  \frac{b}{2a} = \frac{1}{2} \quad \Rightarrow \quad
  \frac{b}{a} = \frac{1}{2} \cdot \frac{1}{2a} = \frac{1}{4a}
  $$

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  We can solve for $\frac{b}{a}$ by isolating the variable on one side of the equation. 
  We can isolate $\frac{b}{a}$ by multiplying both sides of the equation $\frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2}$ by $\frac{b}{2a}$.
  Simplifying the left-hand side of the equation gives us $\frac{2a}{b}\cdot \frac{b}{2a} = 1$
  Simplifying the right-hand side of the equation gives us $\frac{1}{2}\cdot \frac{b}{2a} = \frac{b}{4a}$
  Thus, we have $\frac{b}{4a} = 1$
  Solving for $\frac{b}{a}$, we get $\frac{b}{a} = 4$
